# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Kubelet Components Mapped

**1. Pod Lifecycle Event Generator (PLEG)** 
- **Files**: `pkg/kubelet/pleg/pleg.go` (interface), `pkg/kubelet/pleg/generic.go` (generic implementation), `pkg/kubelet/pleg/evented.go` (event-driven implementation)
- **Key Symbols**: `PodLifecycleEventGenerator`, `GenericPLEG`, `EventedPLEG`, `PodLifecycleEvent`
- Observes container runtime state changes and generates lifecycle events

**2. Container Runtime Interface (CRI) Client**
- **Files**: `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go`, `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_image.go`
- **Key Symbols**: `remoteRuntimeService`, `remoteImageService`
- Provides gRPC client implementation for container runtime communication

**3. Volume Manager**
- **Files**: `pkg/kubelet/volumemanager/volume_manager.go`, `pkg/kubelet/volumemanager/reconciler/reconciler_common.go`, `pkg/kubelet/volumemanager/populator/desired_state_of_world_populator.go`
- **Key Symbols**: `VolumeManager`, `volumeManagerImpl`
- Orchestrates volume attachment, mounting, and lifecycle operations

**4. Device Plugin Manager**
- **Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`, `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/endpoint.go`
- **Key Symbols**: `ManagerImpl`, `Manager`
- Manages device plugins and extended resource allocation

            "content": "11: \n12: This repository contains the client source code for the Container Runtime Interface (CRI).\n13: CRI is a plugin interface which enables kubelet to use a wide variety of container runtimes,\n14: without the need to recompile. CRI consists of a protocol buffers and gRPC API.\n15: Read more about CRI at [kubernetes docs](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/architecture/cri/).\n16: \n17: The repository [kubernetes/cri-client](https://github.com/kubernetes/cri-client) is a mirror of https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/tree/master/staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client.\n18: Please do **not** file issues or submit PRs against the [kubernetes/cri-client](https://github.com/kubernetes/cri-client)\n19: repository as it is readonly, all development is done in [kubernetes/kubernetes](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes).\n20: ",
            "endLine": 20,

          {
            "content": "20: \n21: The [`cri-api` staging repository](https://github.com/kubernetes/cri-api) is\n22: defined in [kubernetes/kubernetes](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes)\n23: and is **only** intended to be used for kubelet to container runtime\n24: interactions, or for node-level troubleshooting using a tool such as `crictl`.\n25: The `cri-api` wraps the [Protobuf protocol definition](https://github.com/kubernetes/cri-api/blob/63929b3/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.proto)\n26: with extra features which can be used directly from other clients as well.\n27: It is **not** a common purpose container runtime API for general use, and is\n28: intended to be Kubernetes-centric. We try to avoid it, but there may be logic\n29: within a container runtime that optimizes for the order or specific parameters\n30: of call(s) that the kubelet makes.\n31: ",
